Background reading if you have been living under a rock.
https://www.palladiummag.com/2023/06/01/complex-systems-wont-survive-the-competence-crisis/

There are countless examples of the competency crisis that have unfolded over the past few years alone. A small, and very incomplete list includes:
>Boeing software forcing planes into a nosedive
>Bridge collapse in Florida the day after it was commissioned
>Several near misses with air traffic at runways throughout America
>The ship that crashed into the bridge and collapsed it
However, we are still in the early stages of this crisis. It will only get worse and will start to impact your life in ways you could have never imagined possible. On the micro scale you’ll notice things just don’t quite work how they used to. Everything will be late, will breakdown more often, and repairs will be simple patch jobs. Medical care will become as risky as the ailment, as it was in the past.
On the macro scale you’ll start to see more frequent, more impactful disasters. Certain systems rely on autistic levels of knowledge, expertise, and experience, which we no longer filter for.
To this end, I believe we need to start decommissioning nuclear power plants. Nuclear disasters don’t just kill people, they make the land unlivable for generations. They have long lasting impacts on people, plant life, and animals. Given we are now in the age of DEI hiring, rather than merit based hiring, it is simply not safe for us to continue the expansion of nuclear energy. It will not be handled by safe and qualified hands. We could be condemning whatever future we have to a nightmare scenario by developing and expanding our nuclear energy supply. And I say this as someone who recognizes the value and potential of nuclear energy. I love it, but given the unfolding crisis it is just too risky to continue.
Discuss.

Anonymous ID:FZUxqxKP Fri 06 Sep 2024 13:11:42 No.480827495  ViewReport
MONTREAL — Brewing company Molson Coors Beverage Co. says it is dropping its diversity, equity and inclusion policies and taking a “broader view” in which all employees know they are welcome.

In an internal memo Molson Coors shared with The Canadian Press, the company says its DEI employee training is complete and that it will no longer have specific “representation goals” in its hiring process.

Article content
As well, the Canadian-American multinational says it will no longer participate in the ranking program by the Human Rights Campaign, an advocacy group that scores companies on how inclusive their workplace practices are toward to the LGBTQ+ community.

Molson Coors says it will instead rely on its own internal metrics as well as employee feedback to develop a “strong workplace where everyone can thrive.”

Human Rights Campaign, which had previously given Molson Coors a perfect rating, did not directly acknowledge the change at the brewery, but noted that some business leaders are turning their backs on commitments to inclusion.
